{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 19:29:59","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:29:59","title":"Singapore-based Volopay wants to be the “Brex of Southeast Asia”","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024893","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><div id=\"attachment_2024894\" style=\"width: 778px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024894\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2024894\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"512\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024894\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/volopay\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"volopay\">Volopay <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> founders Rajith Shaji and Rajesh Raikwar</p></div></p>\n<p>Small- to medium-sized companies that do a lot of international business have to deal with two big headaches: high foreign exchange fees and corporate expense tracking. <a href=\"https://www.volopay.co/\">Volopay</a>, a Singapore-based financial tech startup with offices in Bangalore, wants to help by integrating prepaid multi-currency corporate cards, expense tracking and accounting tools into one free-to-use platform.</p>\n<p>Volopay is currently taking part in Y Combinator and is also part of Antler and Nium’s Bolt, two other accelerator programs. It now has about 40 clients in Singapore, mostly tech startups like Dathena, Tookitaki and Appknox, and plans to launch in Indonesia and Australia within the next six months.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The company was founded last year by chief executive officer Rajith Shaji and chief technology officer Rajesh Raikwar, who met while working at MoneySmart, a financial services comparison platform. Before joining MoneySmart, Shaji also held positions at <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/aax-b20d\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"aax-b20d\">fintech <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> companies like CompareAsiaGroup, MatchMove and BankBazaar.com.</p>\n<p>Shaji spent most of his time working in India, but often traveled to offices abroad. Dealing with corporate expenses after every trip was a &#8220;nightmare,&#8221; Shaji told TechCrunch.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Each time I went back home, I had to make a list of all my expenses on behalf of the company. First of all, it often ran up to a few thousand dollars and I had to put in all these receipts and everything,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>Shaji did not have access to most of the accounting software used by the companies&#8217; accounting departments and communicating with them across different time zones made the process even more cumbersome and time-consuming.</p>\n<p>Volopay addresses those issues by combining prepaid multi-currency corporate cards (available as physical or virtual cards), domestic and international bank transfers, automated payments, and expense and accounting software on one platform. Volopay&#8217;s app lets employees ask for more funds for their prepaid cards from managers, who can approve or reject the request instantly.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg\"><img class=\"alignright wp-image-2024895 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg 1600w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Shaji said this saves companies money on foreign exchange fees, which are typically about 3% of a transaction on a traditional credit card, and gives them real-time visibility into spending.</p>\n<p>Volopay is free to use and earns money through the interchange fees credit cards charge merchants. Interchange fees also enable Volopay to offer perks like cashback deals.</p>\n<p>Shaji said the company aspires to be the &#8220;Brex of Southeast Asia.&#8221; Like Brex, it offers an alternative to traditional financial services for startups and other small- to mid-sized businesses. But it needs to compete with several companies that also want to solve some of the same problems, like high fees for cross-border banking and corporate expense tracking. For example, Transferwise and Revolut both have operations in Singapore, while Neat and Aspire, based in Hong Kong and Singapore respectively, offer online business accounts.</p>\n<p>Shaji said Volopay&#8217;s integration of multiple services on one platform gives it a competitive edge, adding that a better comparison to his startup is YouTrip, a multi-currency wallet for consumers that is popular in Singapore.</p>\n<p>With accounts linked to a prepaid Mastercard, YouTrip users can make payments in 150 currencies without fees and it also supports in-app foreign currency exchanges. When explaining Volopay to potential clients, Shaji often refers to it as &#8220;YouTrip for companies.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;YouTrip is a well-known brand [in Singapore], everyone knows they can load their money on it and save money on foreign exchange,&#8221; he said. Volopay gives the same functionality to companies, with accounting software added.</p>\n<p>Volopay currently focuses on serving small businesses with 25 or more employees, especially tech startups that are scaling their operations and therefore need to manage increasing numbers of online payments and expenses. Shaji said Volopay has also signed up several marketing agencies, because many work on multiple projects, and therefore have to juggle multiple budgets at once.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Shu","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn76@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596108600892_bd6104540375ab8d.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?w=680":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn19@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596108618059_0bab0625e5829c77.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn72@2020_6/2020-07-30/1596108600778_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn59@2020_5/2020-07-30/1596108619261_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn47@2020_1/2020-07-30/1596108618668_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=H_z17WAvDGo:M3XyfqR7330:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn95@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596108619816_439d3412b11b0b0f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=H_z17WAvDGo:M3XyfqR7330:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn43@2020_2/2020-07-30/1596108619081_424735f8213f8335.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn75@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596108619649_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/H_z17WAvDGo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn59@2020_1/2020-07-30/1596108617993_b57045ea393de1a5.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 19:29:59","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:29:59","title":"Apple’s App Store commission structure called into question in antitrust hearing","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024333","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> CEO Tim Cook defended the company’s App Store commission structure in his sworn testimony before the House Antitrust Subcommittee on Wednesday. He claimed the majority of the apps pay no commission at all, with others paying either 15 or 30 percent, based on the specifics of their particular situation. He said developers were all treated equally and that Apple wouldn&#8217;t raise commissions, because it had to compete for developer interest in its platform as well.</p>\n<p>But the documents shared by the House subcommittee as part of their investigation indicate that exceptions to Apple&#8217;s rules have been made &#8212; notably, with Amazon&#8217;s Prime Video app. In addition, Apple may have never raised commissions, but discussions weren&#8217;t off the table. It had once even considered raising commissions to 40% in particular situations.</p>\n<p>The lawmakers had come to the hearing armed with internal Apple emails and interviews from App Store developers who argued that Apple doesn’t uniformly enforce its rules and plays favorites. But their questioning of Cook over App Store fees, combined with a format that limited execs’ ability to respond at length, initially seemed to reveal little in terms of new information about Apple&#8217;s practices.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>For instance, when asked directly about how the App Store worked, Cook simply restated the store&#8217;s published rules — that is, for app developers who have to pay commissions, they pay only 15 or 30 percent. The current guidelines require 30% for apps selling digital goods or services, with a drop to 15% in year two for subscription apps. The rules also document a carve-out for “reader” apps like audiobook apps, streaming services, news publications, and other competitive products which have the option of forgoing in-app purchases.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p>Cook also squeezed in a mention about how the vast majority of App Store apps, 84%, pay nothing to Apple in commissions. It&#8217;s the remaining 16% that pay, he noted.</p>\n<p>And when asked if Apple was the sole gatekeeper as to what gets published on the App Store, Cook agreed that it was — given that the App Store was a “feature of the iPhone, much like the Camera and the chip is.” He clarified that Apple’s control over apps only extended to native software applications, not web apps, but denied Apple treated developers unfairly.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We treat every developer the same. We have open and transparent rules,&#8221; Cook said, in his testimony. &#8220;It&#8217;s a rigorous process, because we care so deeply about privacy and security and quality. We do look at every app before it goes on,” he added.</p>\n<p>But emails in 2016 between Apple SVP Eddy Cue and Amazon CEO Jeff Bezos, shared <a href=\"https://judiciary.house.gov/uploadedfiles/27753.pdf\">here</a> on the House Judiciary Committee&#8217;s website, indicate that Apple, in fact, appears to have negotiated a special deal with Amazon over its Amazon Prime Video app for iOS and Apple TV.  In an email dated Nov. 2016 &#8212; before the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/12/06/amazon-prime-video-finally-lands-on-apple-tv/\">2017 launch of the Prime Video tvOS app</a> &#8212;  Apple agreed to take only a 15% revenue share for customers that signed up in the app using Apple&#8217;s payment mechanism. (Typically, subscription apps don&#8217;t drop from 30% to 15% until year two.)</p>\n<p>Apple this April confirmed <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/01/in-a-significant-change-apple-customers-can-now-buy-or-rent-titles-directly-in-the-prime-video-app/\"> it had a special program for Prime Video</a> and a small handful of other apps, which were subscription video entertainment providers. The program allowed those companies to rent or sell movies and TV shows to customers using the payment methods the companies already had on file, as well as more deeply integrate with Siri. But Apple hadn&#8217;t said that this special program would include a reduced commission on subscriptions or any other in-app upsells, as these emails confirm were points of discussion.</p>\n<p>This wouldn&#8217;t be the first time Apple saw its commission structure as having some room to flex.</p>\n<p>When Cook was questioned as to whether there was anything that could stop Apple from raising commissions to, say, 50%, the CEO responded that Apple had never increased commissions since day one. He also argued, when asked if anything could stop it from doing so, that competition for developer interest would stop it from raising its cut.</p>\n<p>&#8220;There is a competition for developers, just like there&#8217;s a competition for customers. And so the competition for developers &#8212; they write their apps for Android or Windows or Xbox or Playstation,&#8221; said Cook. &#8220;We have fierce competition on the developer side and the customer side which is essentially &#8212; it&#8217;s so competitive, I would describe it as a street fight for market share in the smartphone business,&#8221; he added.</p>\n<p>But in internal emails from 2011, Apple did discuss raising commissions &#8212; all the way to 40% for the first year of recurring subscriptions. &#8220;I think we may be leaving money on the table if we just asked for about 30% of the first year of sub,&#8221; Cue had written at the time.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\" lang=\"en\">Documents from the Hearing on “Online Platforms and Market Power: Examining the Dominance of Amazon, Apple, Facebook and Google&#8221; <a href=\"https://t.co/42o2Ye13jI\">pic.twitter.com/42o2Ye13jI</a></p>\n<p>— House Judiciary Dems (@HouseJudiciary) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/HouseJudiciary/status/1288567281396711426?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 29, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>Of course, Apple didn&#8217;t go so far as to actually make that change in the years that passed. But these emails indicate there&#8217;s more to Apple&#8217;s thinking &#8212; and its discussions around the commission structure &#8212; than the even playing field Cook testified to.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/tech-antitrust-hearing\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tech-antitrust-hearing-banner.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=XlpdmL_I7xo:ABONlZk9tJQ:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a 19:29:59","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:29:59","title":"In antitrust hearing, Zuckerberg admits Facebook has copied its competition","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024146","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">At the House Antitrust Subcommittee hearings this afternoon, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/facebook\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"facebook\">Facebook <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> CEO Mark Zuckerberg was directly questioned about his company&#8217;s strategy of copying competitors&#8217; app and features, and even threatening to do so as a negotiation tactic amid M&#38;A discussions. In his response, Zuckerberg was forced to admit the obvious: that Facebook, he said, has &#8220;certainly adapted features that others have led in.&#8221;</p>\n<p>However, he denied any characterization claiming Facebook used such tactics in an anti-competitive way &#8212; for example, to pressure a company to sell to Facebook instead of trying to compete with it.</p>\n<p>In one particular line of questioning between Rep. Pramila Jayapal (D-WA) and Facebook&#8217;s CEO, she asked specifically about the company&#8217;s billion-dollar <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2012/04/09/facebook-to-acquire-instagram-for-1-billion/\">acquisition of Instagram in 2012</a>. The M&#38;A deal had been <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/29/facebook-instagram-deal-illegal-nadler/\">already been brought up repeatedly</a> throughout the hearing as an example of Facebook buying its way into expanded market power.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Jayapal led into the questions around <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/instagram\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"instagram\">Instagram <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> by first painting a picture of a company where execs agreed that copying from other apps was a viable business strategy.</p>\n<p>She specifically referenced <a href=\"https://judiciary.house.gov/uploadedfiles/0005351500053516.pdf\">emails from 2012</a> between Zuckerberg and Facebook COO Sheryl Sandberg where the CEO had written that by moving faster, Facebook could &#8220;prevent our competitors from getting footholds.&#8221; Sandberg had responded that &#8220;it is hard not to agree it that is better to do more and move faster, especially if that means you don&#8217;t have competitors build products that takes some of our users.&#8221; A PM had also chimed in that they would love to see Facebook being &#8220;even more aggressive and nimble&#8221; in copying competitors, Jayapal noted.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024043\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024043\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2024043\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Mark Zuckerberg\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg 1920w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024043\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch/screenshot</p></div></p>\n<p>The emails had hinted at the birth of Facebook&#8217;s strategy around copying its competition, as they detailed meetings between a high-level Facebook employee and the Renren founders as well as Robin Li from China&#8217;s Baidu.</p>\n<p>The employee had learned of the overall culture of cloning products quickly in the Chinese app market.  Renren had built its own version of Pinterest and Tumblr, the emails said, as well as games, a music product and more. And Tencent QQ had then just released a messaging app similar to the walkie-talkie app Voxer in the U.S. It was pointed out that maybe it was easier to move quickly because these companies were &#8220;just copying other people,&#8221; the email suggested.</p>\n<p>Zuckerberg had forwarded the email to Sandberg, noting &#8220;you&#8217;ll probably find this interesting and agree.&#8221; And she did.</p>\n<p>Under questioning, Zuckerberg declined to say how many companies Facebook had copied since the 2012 email exchange, bristling that he didn&#8217;t agree with the premise of the question.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Our job is to make sure that we build the best services for people to connect with all the people they care about. And a lot of that is done by innovating and by building new things&#8230;,&#8221; he began, before being cut off.</p>\n<p>Jayapal then asked if Facebook had ever threatened to clone a product from another company while attempting to acquire it.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Not that I recall,&#8221; Zuckerberg said.</p>\n<p>However, it seems Facebook had threatened to use <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2012/05/24/facebook-camera/\">its &#8220;Facebook Camera&#8221; app</a> against Instagram ahead of the latter&#8217;s acquisition, Jayapal noted. In a chat with Instagram co-founder Kevin Systrom, Zuckerberg said Facebook was developing its own photo strategy, and how we engage now will also determine how much we&#8217;re partners versus competitors down the line, she explained. <a href=\"https://www.scribd.com/document/470826155/House-Judiciary-Facebook-text-log-between-Mark-Zuckerberg-and-Kevin-Systrom\">In an email chain</a>, Zuckerberg had told Systrom that &#8220;at some point, you&#8217;ll need to figure out how you actually want to work with us.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The Instagram founder had also <a href=\"https://www.scribd.com/document/470826365/House-Judiciary-Chat-log-between-Kevin-Systrom-and-Matt-Cohler\">confided in an investor</a> that he felt Zuckerberg&#8217;s comments were a threat, Jayapal said, and was concerned that Facebook would go into &#8220;destroy mode&#8221; if he didn&#8217;t sell Instagram.</p>\n<p>Zuckerberg didn&#8217;t deny the conversation, but disagreed again with the characterization, saying it was clear that this was a space the two companies would compete in.</p>\n<p>Jayapal asked also if a similar tactic was used against Snapchat in its attempts to acquire the company.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I don&#8217;t remember those specific conversations,&#8221; Zuckerberg responded. &#8220;But that was also an area where was very clear that we were going to be building something,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>Jayapal concluded her time by stating that she did believe Facebook was a monopoly because of this and other behavior.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I think the question again here is when the dominant platform threatens as potential rivals, that should not be a normal business practice. Facebook is a case study, in my opinion, in monopoly power because your company harvests and monetizes our data, and then your company uses that data to spy on competitors, and to copy acquire and kill rivals,&#8221; she said.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/tech-antitrust-hearing\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tech-antitrust-hearing-banner.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Sy1LV79Vu3w:-dRkOfV029I:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img Jerry Nadler declared, &#8220;Facebook saw Instagram as a powerful threat that could siphon business away from Facebook so rather than compete with it, Facebook bought it.&#8221; And Rep. spent their earliest days in <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/y-combinator\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"y-combinator\">Y Combinator&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> accelerator program.</p>\n<p>Steering the ship at Y Combinator today is its president, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" In the earliest weeks of the pandemic, this meant quickly shifting their otherwise in-person demo day online; later, it meant adapting the entire accelerator program to be completely remote.</p>\n<p>While still relatively new to the president seat, Ralston is by no means new to YC. He joined the accelerator <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2012/01/27/y-combinator-names-seasoned-entrepreneur-geoff-ralston-as-its-newest-partner/\">as a partner in 2012</a>, and his edtech-focused accelerator <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/02/10/y-combinator-absorbs-edtech-accelerator-imagine-k12-creating-specialized-vertical/\">Imagine K12</a> was fully merged into YC&#8217;s operations in 2016.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=p8EihxbE9bw:DvuA0i8MaZY:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img 19:29:59","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:29:59","title":"Amazon’s hardware business doesn’t escape Congressional scrutiny","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024313","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">While much of today&#8217;s <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/29/big-tech-cicilline-pandemic-antitrust-hearing/\">Congressional grilling into the anticompetitive practices of the big tech giants</a> focused on their core businesses, Amazon&#8217;s hardware also came in for close inspection during the hours-long interrogation.</p>\n<p>It was a small but significant exchange, because it touched on the breadth of the company&#8217;s services and how dominance in one area can mean potentially anti-competitive behavior in another part of the tech giant&#8217;s business.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"TskXjdQr1o\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/29/big-tech-cicilline-pandemic-antitrust-hearing/\">Lawmakers argue that big tech stands to benefit from the pandemic and must be regulated</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Lawmakers argue that big tech stands to benefit from the pandemic and must be regulated&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/29/big-tech-cicilline-pandemic-antitrust-hearing/embed/#?secret=TskXjdQr1o\" data-secret=\"TskXjdQr1o\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>For Maryland&#8217;s Representative Jamie Raskin, both Amazon&#8217;s best-selling <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B07R1CXKN7?tag=mh0b-20&#38;hvadid=78271518759182&#38;hvqmt=e&#38;hvbmt=be&#38;hvdev=c&#38;ref=pd_sl_2g7cb1h5zl_e\">Echo</a> and the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/b/?ie=UTF8&#38;node=8521791011&#38;tag=mh0b-20&#38;hvadid=78615109214187&#38;hvqmt=e&#38;hvbmt=be&#38;hvdev=c&#38;ref=pd_sl_18xa831llk_e\">Fire TV devices</a> became targets thanks to recent reporting on the company&#8217;s business practices and negotiations regarding both devices.</p>\n<p>The Echo is the company&#8217;s foray into the smart home market that&#8217;s widely seen as the next major battleground in consumer technology. It&#8217;s one of the most widely adopted pieces of Amazon&#8217;s technology and has captured about 60% of the smart home market, according to Raskin.</p>\n<p>The congressman hammered Bezos on two points about the Echo. The first was the company&#8217;s pricing scheme which had the Echo priced well below the cost to produce the device making it all but impossible for other tech companies to compete.</p>\n<p>The Echo&#8217;s wide adoption has also led Amazon to engage in other anti-competitive behavior, Raskin asserted — some of which was outlined in previous questioning from Colorado Rep. Ken Buck <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/amazon-tech-startup-echo-bezos-alexa-investment-fund-11595520249\">citing a Wall Street Journal report</a> that Amazon had used its investment unit focused on its Echo product and Alexa voice assistant to copy technology coming from small startup companies.</p>\n<p>But beyond its appropriation of another company&#8217;s intellectual property, Amazon also used the Echo platform to promote its own products over competitors when customers used its voice services.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Is Alexa trained to favor Amazon products?&#8221; Raskin asked.</p>\n<p>Bezos responded that he wasn&#8217;t sure if Amazon had specifically trained the Alexa to default to Amazon services or to promote the company&#8217;s own brand of products, but that he wouldn&#8217;t be surprised. &#8220;It wouldn&#8217;t surprise me if Alexa sometimes does promote our own products,&#8221; the Amazon chief executive said.</p>\n<p>Raskin also took Bezos to task for the company&#8217;s recent negotiations with WarnerMedia, the production studio, streaming service, and network giant. Specifically, he was concerned with how negotiations around the distribution of WarnerMedia&#8217;s HBO Max service on the company&#8217;s Fire TV devices included discussions around Amazon&#8217;s access to WarnerMedia productions.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;You’re not only asking for financial terms but also for content from Warner Media,&#8221; Raskin said. &#8220;Is it fair to use your gatekeeper status role in the streaming device market to promote your position as a competitor in the video streaming market with respect to content?&#8221;</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Bezos responded that the negotiations were &#8220;normal commerce,&#8221; but Raskin tried to make the case that the negotiations over access to the Fire was yet another way in which the company&#8217;s leverage in one market impacted its ability to exercise unfair advantage against a competitor in a different industry. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You’re using your control over access to people’s living rooms essentially,&#8221; Raskin said. &#8220;You’re using that to obtain leverage in terms of getting creative content that you want. Are you essentially converting power in one domain into power in another domain where it doesn’t belong?&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>The comments and line of inquiry from Raskin were part of an intense bout of questioning that seemed to hone in on the purported topic of the hearings — the anti-competitive and potentially monopolistic power wielded by four of the nation&#8217;s largest tech companies. Facebook, Apple and Alphabet were all raked over the Congressional coals in bouts of questioning, but it seemed that the most sustained criticism on anti-competitive behavior was reserved for Bezos and Amazon.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5KhJGyDRBc\"><p><a class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-name\">Nitesh Dudhia</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-title\" style=\"display: block;\">Contributor</span>\n\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t\t\t<div d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"/>\t</svg>\n\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\t<a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/ndudhia/\">Nitesh Dudhia</a> is co-founder and CBO of <a href=\"https://www.aikonlabs.com/\">Aikon Labs Pvt Ltd</a>. Nitesh has worked on market opportunity identification, business planning and strategy formulation and execution for digital transformation.\t</div>\n\t\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">As offices worldwide shift to remote work, our interactions with customers and colleagues have evolved in tandem. Professionals who once relied on face-to-face communication and firm handshakes must now close deals in a world where both are rare. Coworkers we once sat beside every day are now only available over Slack and Zoom, changing the nature of internal communication as well.</p>\n<p>While this new reality presents a challenge, the advancement of key technologies allows us to not just adapt, but thrive. We are now on the precipice of the biggest revolution in workplace communication since the invention of the telephone.</p>\n<p>It’s not enough to simply accept the new status quo, particularly as the overall economic climate remains tenuous. Artificial intelligence has much to offer in improving the way we speak to one another in the social distance era, and has already seen wide adoption in certain areas. Much of this algorithmic work has gone on behind the scenes of our most-used apps, such as Google Meet’s <a href=\"https://venturebeat.com/2020/06/08/google-meet-noise-cancellation-ai-cloud-denoiser-g-suite/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://venturebeat.com/2020/06/08/google-meet-noise-cancellation-ai-cloud-denoiser-g-suite/&#38;source=gmail&#38;ust=1596129574505000&#38;usg=AFQjCNGlCgw1ZAFJu-N8gT1aOU_JN3UzMA\">noise-canceling</a> technology, which uses an AI to mute certain extraneous sounds on video calls. Other advances work in real-time right before our eyes — like Zoom’s myriad virtual backgrounds, or the automatic transcription and translation technology built into most video conferencing apps.</p>\n<p>This kind of technology has helped employees realize that, despite the unprecedented shift to remote work, digital conversations do not just strive to recreate the in-person experience — rather, they can improve upon the way we communicate entirely.</p>\n<p>It’s estimated that <a href=\"https://www.upwork.com/press/2020/06/11/fourth-annual-future-workforce-report/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.upwork.com/press/2020/06/11/fourth-annual-future-workforce-report/&#38;source=gmail&#38;ust=1596129574505000&#38;usg=AFQjCNHx5KQFioY8QvrK8Z38Eaa0lcQOyQ\">65%</a> of the workforce will be working remotely within the next five years. With a more hands-on approach to AI — that is, using the technology to actually augment everyday communications — workers can gain insight into concepts, workflows and ideas that would otherwise go unnoticed.</p>\n<h2>Your customer service experience</h2>\n<p>Roughly <a href=\"https://priceonomics.com/companies-collect-a-lot-of-data-but-how-much-do/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://priceonomics.com/companies-collect-a-lot-of-data-but-how-much-do/&#38;source=gmail&#38;ust=1596129574505000&#38;usg=AFQjCNGfSKaAgpoIzS1IdF9nnKza-7j0xQ\">55%</a> of the data companies collect falls into the category of &#8220;dark data&#8221;: information that goes completely unused, kept on an internal server until it’s eventually wiped. Any company with a customer service department is invariably growing their stock of dark data with every chat log, email exchange and recorded call.</p>\n<p>When a customer phones in with a query or complaint, they’re told early on that their call &#8220;may be recorded for quality assurance purposes.&#8221; Given how cheap data storage has become, there’s no &#8220;maybe&#8221; about it. The question is what to do with this data.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Labs","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2023975","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">After raising $15 million in financing from one of technology&#8217;s most successful global investment firms, the Los Angeles-based consumer goods rental company <a href=\"https://www.joymode.com/\">Joymode</a> is selling itself to an early-stage retail investment firm out of New York, <a href=\"https://www.xrclabs.com/\">XRC Labs</a>.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/joymode\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"joymode\">Joymode&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> founder <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/joe-fernandez\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"joe-fernandez\">Joe Fernandez <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> will continue on as an advisor to Joymode as the company moves to pivot its business to focus on retail partnerships.</p>\n<p>The relationship with <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/xrclabs\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"xrclabs\">XRC Labs&#8217; <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Pano Anthos began after a small pilot integration between <a href=\"https://www.pe.com/2019/11/15/rentals-by-joymode-debuts-in-temecula-walmart-heres-how-it-works/\">Joymode and Walmart</a> launched in late 2019. &#8220;[It] became obvious that we should go all in on retail partnerships,&#8221; according to Fernandez. And as the company cast about for partners to pursue the strategy, Anthos and his firm, XRC, kept being mentioned, Fernandez said.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The precise terms of the deal with XRC Labs were undisclosed, but Joymode will become a wholly owned business of XRC and could potentially return to market to raise additional funds from additional investors, according to Fernandez.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We could never crack growth at the scale we needed,&#8221; said Fernandez of the company&#8217;s initial business. &#8220;From day one, my belief was Joymode was going to be huge or dead. We grew, but given the cost structure of our business it put a lot of pressure on the business to grow exponentially fast. Everyone loved the idea but the actual growth was slower than we needed it to be.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Though Joymode wasn&#8217;t a success, Fernandez said he can&#8217;t fault his investors or his team. &#8220;We got to iterate through every possible idea we had. Literally every idea we had was exhausted&#8230; We failed and that&#8217;s a bummer, but we got a fair shot,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>What remains of the company is an inventory management system on the back end and a service that will allow any retailer to get involved in the rental business going forward.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Part of the thesis was that by making things available for rental, people would want to do more stuff,&#8221; said Fernandez, but what happened was that consumers needed additional reasons to use the company&#8217;s service, and there weren&#8217;t enough events to drive demand.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;I believe that the inventory management system we made was incredible and it will be a standard for retailers doing rentals going forward,&#8221; he said. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> As the company turned to retailers, the rental option became a way to generate revenue through additional products. &#8220;All the accessories that made the event even better,&#8221; said Fernandez. &#8220;Add-ons, try before you buy, experiential things that are just much more complete in a retail environment.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>At Joymode, the problem was that the company was owning the inventory, which created a high fixed cost. &#8220;We never felt confident with the growth in LA to justify the expense of opening in another city,&#8221; Fernandez said. &#8220;<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If we had cracked user acquisition in LA we would have rolled it out in a bunch of places.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>Ultimately, Joymode members saved $50 million by using Joymode to rent products rather than buying them. In all, the company acquired 2,000 unique products &#8212; from beach and camping equipment to video games, virtual reality headsets to cooking appliances. On a given weekend, roughly 30,000 products would ship from the company&#8217;s warehouse to locations across Southern California.</p>\n<p>At XRC Labs, a firm launched in 2015 to support the consumer goods and brand space, Joymode will complement an accelerator that raises between $6 million and $9 million every two years and manages a growth fund that could reach $50 million in assets under management.</p>\n<p>For Anthos, the best corollary to Joymode&#8217;s business could be the rental business at Home Depot. &#8220;Home Depot&#8217;s rental business is over $1 billion per year,&#8221; Anthos said. &#8220;There&#8217;s going to be this enormous component of our society and for them renting will be not just a more sustainable but reasonable option. They&#8217;re going to want to rent because they don&#8217;t want to own it.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Joymode was backed by TenOneTen, Wonder, Struck Ventures, Homebrew and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/naspers\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"naspers\">Naspers <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> (now Prosus).</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=5uI47bhga00:DdfbB6JvdOc:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img 19:29:59","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:29:59","title":"Google’s Sundar Pichai grilled over ‘destroying anonymity on the internet’","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024118","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/sundar-pichai\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"sundar-pichai\">Sundar Pichai <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> faced an awkward line of enquiry during today&#8217;s House Antitrust Subcommittee hearing related to its 2007 acquisition of adtech platform DoubleClick, and how it went on to renege on an original promise to lawmakers and regulators that it would not (nor could not) merge <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/doubleclick\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"doubleclick\">DoubleClick <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> data with Google account data &#8212; automagically doing just that almost a decade later.</p>\n<p>By linking internet users&#8217; browsing data, as harvested via the DoubleClick cookie, to Google accounts it was able to join the dots of user identities, (Gmail) email data, search history, location data and so on (Google already having collapsed the privacy policies of separate products, to join up all that activity) with its users&#8217; wider internet browsing activity &#8212; vastly expanding its ability to profile and target people with behavioral ads.</p>\n<p>Agency for Google users to prevent this massive privacy intrusion, there was none.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Rep. Val Demings contended that by combining DoubleClick cookie data and Google account data Google had essentially destroyed user privacy on the internet. And &#8212; importantly, given the domestic antitrust scrutiny the company now faces &#8212; that that had only been possible because of the market power Google had amassed.</p>\n<p>&#8220;When Google proposed the merger alarm bells were raised about the access to data Google would have &#8212; specifically the ability to connect a user&#8217;s personal identity with their browsing activity,&#8221; said Demings, before zooming in to hammer Pichai on another tech giant broken data privacy promise.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Google&#8230; committed to Congress and to the antitrust enforcers that the deal would not reduce user privacy. Google chief&#8217;s legal advisor testified before the Senate Antitrust Subcommittee that Google wouldn&#8217;t be able to merge this data. Even if it wanted to, given contractual restrictions. But in June of 2016 Google went ahead and merged this data anyway &#8212; effectively destroying anonymity on the internet,&#8221; she explained.</p>\n<p>Demings then pressed Pichai on whether he personally signed off on the privacy-hostile move, given he became CEO of Google in 2015.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RepValDemings?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@RepValDemings</a> crushes it on what was my burning question for Google by probing 2016 cookie/data merge. Here is the press report. It&#39;s also known as question #106 by Texas AG <a href=\"https://twitter.com/KenPaxtonTX?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@KenPaxtonTX</a>. Republican for those who think these concerns are partisan. <a href=\"https://t.co/WV8qj2Iepk\">https://t.co/WV8qj2Iepk</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/JgSYgojtEX\">pic.twitter.com/JgSYgojtEX</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Jason Kint (@jason_kint) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/jason_kint/status/1288555619239288832?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 29, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p>Pichai hesitated before attempting a bland response &#8212; only to be interrupted by Demings pressing him again: &#8220;Did you sign off on the decision or not?&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;I &#8212; I reviewed at a high level all the important decisions we make,&#8221; he said, after a micro pause.</p>\n<p>He then segwayed in search of more comfortable territory, starting into Google&#8217;s usual marketing spiel &#8212; about how it &#8220;deeply cares about the privacy and security of our users&#8221;.</p>\n<p>Demings was having none of it. The U-turn had enabled Google to combine a user&#8217;s search and browsing history, location data and information from emails stored in Gmail, she said, blasting it &#8220;absolutely staggering&#8221;.</p>\n<p>She then referenced an email from a DoubleClick exec who had told the committee it was &#8220;exactly the kind of user reduction in privacy that users&#8217; founders had previously worried would lead to a backlash&#8221;.</p>\n<p>&#8220;&#8216;They were unwavering on the policy due to philosophical reasons. Which is Larry [Page] and Sergey [Brin] fundamentally not wanting users associated with a cross-site cookie. They were also worried about a privacy storm, as well as damage to Google&#8217;s brand&#8217;,&#8221; she said, quoting directly from the email from the unnamed DoubleClick exec.</p>\n<p>&#8220;So in 2007 Google&#8217;s founders feared making this change because they knew it would upset their users &#8212; but in 2016 Google didn&#8217;t seem to care,&#8221; Demings went on, before putting it to Pichai that what had changed between 2007 and 2016 is that Google gained &#8220;enormous market power&#8221;.</p>\n<p>&#8220;So while Google had to care about user privacy in 2007 it no longer had to in 2016 &#8212; would you agree that what changed was Google gained enormous market power?&#8221; she asked.</p>\n<p>The <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/alphabet\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"alphabet\">Alphabet <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Google CEO responded by asking for a chance &#8220;to explain&#8221; &#8212; and then rattling off a list of controls Google offers users so they can try and shrink how it tracks them, further claiming it makes it &#8220;very easy&#8221; for people to control what it does with their information. (Some EU data regulators have <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/19/french-court-slaps-down-googles-appeal-against-57m-gdpr-fine/\">taken a very different view of Google&#8217;s &#8216;transparency&#8217;</a>, however.)</p>\n<p>&#8220;We today make it very easy for users to be in control of their data,&#8221; claimed Pichai. &#8220;We have simplified their settings, they can turn ads personalization on or off &#8212; we have combined most of activity settings into three groupings. We remind users to go do a privacy check up. One billion users have done so.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Demings, sounding unimpressed, cut him off again &#8212; saying: &#8220;I am concerned that Google&#8217;s bait and switch with DoubleClick is part of a broader pattern where Google buys up companies for the purposes of surveilling Americans and because of Google&#8217;s dominance users have no choice but to surrender.&#8221;</p>\n<p>She went on to contend that &#8220;more user data means more money&#8221; for Google.</p>\n<p>Pichai had a go at denying that &#8212; starting an answer with the claim that &#8220;in general that&#8217;s not true&#8221; before Demings repeated the contention: &#8220;So you&#8217;re saying that more user data does not mean the more money that Google can collect?&#8221;</p>\n<p>That was easier for Pichai to sidestep. &#8220;Most of the data we collect is to help users and provide personalized experiences back&#8221;, he shot back, neatly avoiding the key point that the access Google has given itself to people&#8217;s data by cross linking their web browsing with Google IDs and product activity enables the tech giant to generate massive profits via targeting them with creepy ads, which in turn makes up the vast majority of Alphabet&#8217;s profit.</p>\n<p>But with that Demings&#8217; five minutes were up &#8212; although the hearing continues. You can tune in <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ROTyg-IiwG0&#38;feature=youtu.be\">here</a>.</p>\n<p>Shortly later in the session, facing further questions around ad data, Pichai noted that Google no longer uses data from Gmail for ad targeting &#8212; although this change is relatively recent (<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/06/23/google-has-all-the-data-it-needs-will-stop-scanning-gmail-inboxes/\">June 2017</a>).</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/tech-antitrust-hearing\"><img 19:29:59","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:29:59","title":"Samsung’s second-quarter profit grew 23% year-over-year, thanks to strong chip demand","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024879","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https://www.samsung.com/us/aboutsamsung/home/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Samsung Electronics</a> sounded a cautiously optimistic note in its <a href=\"https://images.samsung.com/is/content/samsung/p5/global/ir/docs/2020_2Q_conference_eng.pdf\">earnings report today</a>. The company is continuing to deal with the fallout of the COVID-19 pandemic, but its memory business was fortified by demand for DRAM chips as data centers adapted to an increase in remote work and education.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/samsung-electronics\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"samsung-electronics\">Samsung Electronics <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> will launch new models of its flagship smartphones, including the Galaxy Note and a foldable device, at its online Galaxy Unpacked event on August 5, but will also focus on increasing sales of low- to mid-priced phones, which it expects to drive revenue during the rest of the year.</p>\n<p>Second-quarter operating profit grew 26% from the previous quarter, and 23% year-over-year to 8.15 trillion won (about $6.84 billion), due largely to more sales of DRAM chips. Revenue fell 4% from the previous quarter, and 6% year-over-year, to 53 trillion won, while net profit rose 7% to 5.6 trillion won. Samsung said revenue was impacted by lower sales of smartphones and other devices, but some of that was offset by reduced marketing spending and other cost-cutting measures.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Rr0b3GEI7H\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/07/samsung-will-reveal-the-next-galaxy-note-on-august-5/\">Samsung will reveal the next Galaxy Note on August 5</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Samsung will reveal the next Galaxy Note on August 5&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/07/samsung-will-reveal-the-next-galaxy-note-on-august-5/embed/#?secret=Rr0b3GEI7H\" data-secret=\"Rr0b3GEI7H\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The company also acknowledged that it faces intense competition from other smartphone makers. In fact, on the same day that Samsung announced its second-quarter earnings, research firm Canalys <a href=\"https://www.canalys.com/newsroom/Canalys-huawei-samsung-worldwide-smartphone-market-q2-2020?ctid=1556-1195484408fbbb34e0298b96eddb178f\">released a report </a>that said Huawei shipped more smartphones globally than any other vendor in the second-quarter, despite dealing with American government restrictions, displacing Samsung from the top position for the first time.</p>\n<p>On the brighter side, many analysts believe that Samsung, along with TSMC, will benefit from Intel’s recent announcement that<a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-samsung-elec-intel-stocks/samsung-electronics-shares-rally-on-intels-chip-outsourcing-plan-idUSKCN24T0C5\"> it will outsource more semiconductor manufacturing</a>.</p>\n<h3>Remote services drove demand for DRAM chips</h3>\n<p>The company’s semiconductor division was helped by demand for DRAM chips from data centers that need to fortify their online infrastructure to support remote workers and online education. PC demand also remained solid because of low-end laptop sales.</p>\n<p>But sales of chips for mobile devices remained weak as consumers spent less money because of the pandemic. When they did make purchases, they tended to buy low- to mid-end mobile products, which use less powerful chips.</p>\n<h3>A “one-off gain” boosted display revenue</h3>\n<p>Samsung Electronic’s display panel business earnings improved quarter-over-quarter thanks to a “one-off gain” that boosted profits from mobile displays. Samsung did not give details about where the gain came form, but Bloomberg <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-07-29/samsung-beats-estimates-on-recovery-of-chips-and-gadget-sales\">reports</a> it was a compensatory payment of about 1.1 trillion won ($924 million) from Apple after the iPhone maker ordered fewer displays than expected.</p>\n<p>But overall demand for displays was lower as COVID-19 hit smartphone sales. Operating losses were offset slightly by purchases of monitors by people working from home.</p>\n<p>Samsung Electronics said mobile display demand is expected to recover this year as its biggest clients continue to launch new products, despite continuing uncertainties from the pandemic. It also expects orders for mobile and graphic chips to increase as new smartphones and game consoles are released, and anticipates a &#8220;full-fledged rebound in earnings from mobile displays&#8221; by the end of the year, due largely to sales of mid- to low-end smartphones.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/21X5lGlDOfg?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p>NASA is set to launch its newest rover to <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/mars\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"mars\">Mars <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> later this morning. The liftoff is set for 7:50 AM EDT (4:50 AM PDT), with a broadcast beginning at 7:00 AM EDT (4:00 AM PDT). This mission will launch a ULA Atlas V rocket to carry the Perseverance rover to Mars with a trip that will last several months, arriving in February 2021.</p>\n<p>The 2,260-lb rover is equipped with a range of sensors to help it search for signs of past micro organic life on Mars, as well as study the planet&#8217;s amtospheric and geological makeup. It also carries with it a helicopter drone called Ingenuity, which will seek to become the first ever vehicle to take-off and fly within the Mars atmosphere.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Perseverance is a big upgrade over prior rovers in a number of ways. It can cover way more ground operating autonomously per day than any of its predecessors, for instance, which should help it conduct more science than ever before. It&#8217;s also equipped with 19 cameras to provide a full, detailed and high-quality view of its surroundings back to Earth. The rover is also designed to prime the pump for future human Mars exploration (and long-duration human Moon missions), with experiments on board like MOXIE, an instrument that will create oxygen from the CO2 found in Mars&#8217; atmosphere, and will set the stage for a washing machine-sized version to be developed in future that will essentially act as a self-sustaining Mars power source.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1955125\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1955125\" class=\"size-full wp-image-1955125\" The plan is to ultimately combine the efforts of NASA and the European Space Agency to retrieve samples of Martian soil that Perseverance leaves behind in collection canisters using a future target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"microsoft\">Microsoft&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> new <a href=\"https://www.flightsimulator.com/\">Flight Simulator</a>. Without a doubt, it&#8217;s the most beautiful flight simulator yet, and it&#8217;ll make you want to fly low and slow over your favorite cities because &#8212; if you pick the right one &#8212; every street and house will be there in more detail than you&#8217;ve ever seen in a game. Weather effects, day and night cycles, plane models &#8212; it all looks amazing. You can&#8217;t start it up and not fawn over the graphics.</p>\n<p>But the new Flight Simulator is also still very much a work in progress, too, even just a few weeks before the scheduled launch date on August 18. It&#8217;s officially still in beta, so there&#8217;s still time to fix at least some of the issues I list below. Because Microsoft and Asobo Studios, which was responsible for the development of the simulator, are using Microsoft&#8217;s AI tech in Azure to automatically generate much of the scenery based on Microsoft&#8217;s Bing Maps data, you&#8217;ll find a lot of weirdness in the world. There are taxiway lights in the middle of runways, giant hangars and crew buses at small private fields, cars randomly driving across airports, giant trees growing everywhere (while palms often look like giant sticks), bridges that are either under water or big blocks of black over a river &#8212; and there are a lot of sunken boats, too.</p>\n<p>When the system works well, it&#8217;s absolutely amazing. Cities like Barcelona, Berlin, San Francisco, Seattle, New York and others that are rendered using Microsoft&#8217;s photogrammetry method look great &#8212; including and maybe especially at night.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2023932\" style=\"width: 610px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-sedona.gif\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2023932\" class=\"wp-image-2023932 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-sedona.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"338\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2023932\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Microsoft</p></div></p>\n<p>The rendering engine on my i7-9700K with an Nvidia 2070 Super graphics card never let the frame rate drop under 30 frames per second (which is perfectly fine for a flight simulator) and usually hovered well over 40, all with the graphics setting pushed up to the maximum and with a 2K resolution.</p>\n<p>When things don&#8217;t work, though, the effect is stark because it&#8217;s so obvious. Some cities, like Las Vegas, look like they suffered some kind of catastrophe, as if the city was abandoned and nature took over (which in the case of the Vegas Strip doesn&#8217;t sound like such a bad thing, to be honest).</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2023931\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2023931\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2023931\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"513\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg 2019w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg?resize=150,75 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg?resize=300,150 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg?resize=768,385 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg?resize=680,341 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg?resize=1536,769 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-vegas.jpg?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2023931\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>Thankfully, all of this is something that Microsoft and Asobo can fix. They&#8217;ll just need to adjust their algorithms, and because a lot of the data is streamed, the updates should be virtually automatic. The fact that they haven&#8217;t done so yet is a bit of a surprise.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024258\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024258\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2024258\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"646\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg 1613w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg?resize=150,95 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg?resize=300,189 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg?resize=768,484 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg?resize=680,429 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg?resize=1536,968 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-145940.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024258\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>Chances are you&#8217;ll want to fly over your house the day you get Flight Simulator. If you live in the right city (and the right part of that city), you&#8217;ll likely be lucky and actually see your house with its individual texture. But for some cities, including London, for example, the game only shows standard textures, and while Microsoft does a good job at matching the outlines of buildings in cities where it doesn&#8217;t do photogrammetry, it&#8217;s odd that London or Amsterdam aren&#8217;t on that list (though London apparently features a couple of wind turbines in the city center now), while Münster, Germany is.</p>\n<p>Once you get to altitude, all of those problems obviously go away (or at least you won&#8217;t see them). But given the graphics, you&#8217;ll want to spend a lot of time at 2,000 feet or below.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024149\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024149\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2024149\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"550\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg 1962w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg?resize=150,81 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg?resize=300,161 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg?resize=768,412 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg?resize=680,365 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg?resize=1536,824 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-124757.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024149\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>What really struck me in playing the game in its current state is how those graphical inconsistencies set the standard for the rest of the experience. The team says its focus is 100% on making the simulator as realistic as possible, but then the virtual air traffic control often doesn&#8217;t use standard phraseology, for example, or fails to hand you off to the right departure control when you leave a major airport, for example. The airplane models look great and feel pretty close to real (at least for the ones I&#8217;ve flown myself), but some currently show the wrong airspeed, for example. Some planes use modern glass cockpits with the Garmin 1000 and G3X, but those still feel severely limited.</p>\n<p>But let me be clear here. Despite all of this, even in its beta state, Flight Simulator is a technical marvel and it will only get better over time.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2023929\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2023929\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2023929\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"506\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg 1910w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg?resize=150,74 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg?resize=300,148 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg?resize=768,379 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg?resize=680,336 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg?resize=1536,758 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-palm-springs.jpg?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2023929\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>Let&#8217;s walk through the user experience a bit. The install on PC (the Xbox version will come at some point in the future) is a process that downloads a good 90GB so that you can play offline as well. The install process asks you if you are OK with streaming data, too, and that can quickly add up. After reinstalling the game and doing a few flights for screenshots, the game had downloaded about 10GB already &#8212; it adds up quickly and is something you should be aware of if you&#8217;re on a metered connection.</p>\n<p>[gallery ids=\"2024272,2024274,2024275,2024276,2024277,2024278,2024281\"]</p>\n<p>Once past the long install, you&#8217;ll be greeted by a menu screen that lets you start a new flight, go for one of the landing challenges or other activities the team has set up (they are really proud of their Courchevel scenery) and go through the games&#8217; flight training program.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2023926\" style=\"width: 810px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-world-map.gif\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2023926\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2023926\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-world-map.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2023926\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Microsoft</p></div></p>\n<p>That training section walks you through eight activities that will help you get the basics of flying a Cessna 152. Most take fewer than 10 minutes and you&#8217;ll get a bit of a de-brief after, but I&#8217;m not sure it&#8217;s enough to keep a novice from getting frustrated quickly (while more advanced players will just skip this section altogether anyway).</p>\n<p>I mostly spent my time flying the small general aviation planes in the sim, but if you prefer a Boeing 747 or Airbus 320neo, you get that option, too, as well as some turboprops and business jets. I&#8217;ll spend some more time with those before the official launch. All of the planes are beautifully detailed inside and out and except for a few bugs, everything works as expected.</p>\n<p>To actually start playing, you&#8217;ll head for the world map and choose where you want to start your flight. What&#8217;s nice here is that you can pick any spot on your map, not just airports. That makes it easy to start flying over a city, for example. As you zoom into the map, you can see airports and landmarks (where the landmarks are either real sights like Germany&#8217;s Neuschwanstein Castle or cities that have photogrammetry data). If a town doesn&#8217;t have photogrammetry data, it will not appear on the map.</p>\n<p>As of now, the flight planning features are pretty basic. For visual flights, you can go direct or VOR to VOR, and that&#8217;s it. For IFR flights, you choose low or high-altitude airways. You can&#8217;t really adjust any of these, just accept what the simulator gives you. That&#8217;s not really how flight planning works (at the very least you would want to take the local weather into account), so it would be nice if you could customize your route a bit more. Microsoft partnered with NavBlue for airspace data, though the built-in maps don&#8217;t do much with this data and don&#8217;t even show you the vertical boundaries of the airspace you are in.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024150\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024150\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2024150\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"550\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg 1960w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg?resize=150,81 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg?resize=300,161 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg?resize=768,412 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg?resize=680,365 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg?resize=1536,824 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Annotation-2020-07-29-123808-1.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024150\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s always hard to compare the plane models and how they react to the real thing. Best I can tell, at least the single-engine Cessnas that I&#8217;m familiar with mostly handle in the same way I would expect them to in reality. Rudder controls feel a bit overly sensitive by default, but that&#8217;s relatively easy to adjust. I only played with a HOTAS-style joystick and rudder setup. I wouldn&#8217;t recommend playing with a mouse and keyboard, but your mileage may vary.</p>\n<p>Live traffic works well, but none of the general aviation traffic around my local airports seems to show up, even though Microsoft partner FlightAware shows it.</p>\n<p>As for the real/AI traffic in general, the sim does a pretty good job managing that. In the beta, you won&#8217;t really see the liveries of any real airlines yet &#8212; at least for the most part &#8212; I spotted the occasional United plane in the latest builds. Given some of Microsoft&#8217;s own videos, more are coming soon. Except for the built-in models you can fly in the sim, Flight Simulator is still missing a library of other airplane models for AI traffic, though again, I would assume that&#8217;s in the works, too.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024248\" style=\"width: 810px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-night-sf.gif\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024248\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2024248\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/ms-flight-night-sf.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024248\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>We&#8217;re three weeks out from launch. I would expect the team to be able to fix many of these issues and we&#8217;ll revisit all of them for our final review. My frustration with the current state of the game is that it&#8217;s so often so close to perfect that when it falls short of that, it&#8217;s especially jarring because it yanks you out of the experience.</p>\n<p>Don&#8217;t get me wrong, though, flying in FS2020 is already a great experience. Even when there&#8217;s no photogrammetry, cities and villages look great once you get over 3,000 feet or so. The weather and cloud simulation &#8212; in real time &#8212; beats any add-on for today&#8217;s flight simulators. Airports still need work, but having cars drive around and flaggers walking around planes that are pushing back help make the world feel more alive. Wind affects the waves on lakes and oceans (and windsocks on airports). This is truly a next-generation flight simulator.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2023939\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2023939\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2023939\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg 7680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/VL3_NYT_7K_Angkor.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2023939\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Microsoft</p></div></p>\n<p>Microsoft and Asobo have to walk a fine line between making Flight Simulator the sim that hardcore fans want and an accessible game that brings in new players. I&#8217;ve played every version of Flight Simulator since the 90s, so getting started took exactly zero time. My sense is that new players simply looking for a good time may feel a bit lost at first, despite Microsoft adding landing challenges and other more gamified elements to the sim. In a press briefing, the Asobo team regularly stressed that it aimed for realism over anything else &#8212; and I&#8217;m perfectly ok with that. We&#8217;ll have to see if that translates to being a fun experience for casual players, too.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
